## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of population change (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size, which is a classic population dynamics problem. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth models where the growth rate depends on the current population level.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Exponential (Malthusian) growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Unlimited resources, growth rate proportional to population size'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreases logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Population growth with strong Allee effect (minimum viable population)'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Growth as balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth'}
- {'name': 'Power-law growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Generalized density-dependent growth with fractional exponent'}
- {'name': 'Logistic with time-dependent rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth with exponentially changing intrinsic rate'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous form', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent birth with linear mortality'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'Polynomial expansion of density-dependent effects'}
- {'name': 'Delayed feedback approximation', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P * t', 'scenario': 'Growth with time-dependent environmental degradation'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → multiplicative factor (1 - P/K) or rational form 1/(1 + c*P) limiting growth at high population
- Allee effects (low-density decline) → cubic polynomial in P with both positive and negative roots, or (P - threshold) factor
- Logarithmic saturation → log(K/P) term in Gompertz-type models for asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Metabolic scaling → fractional power laws P**c with c between 0 and 1 reflecting allometric biological scaling
- Competing birth-death processes → difference of two positive terms (e.g., c0*P**a - c1*P**b) representing gains minus losses
- Environmental periodicity → trigonometric modulation c0*(1 + c1*sin(c2*t)) multiplying growth terms for seasonal effects
- Regime transitions in time → sigmoid switching functions of t (e.g., 1/(1+exp(-c*(t-t0)))) modulating growth parameters
- Carrying capacity as inflection signature → dP_dt having a maximum at intermediate P values, implying quadratic or dome-shaped dependence on P

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P + 0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P$$

Let $a = 1/5.115 \approx 0.1955$, $b = 1/34.44 \approx 0.02904$

$(-1 + aP)(1 - bP) = -1 + bP + aP - abP^2 = -1 + (a+b)P - abP^2$

So the first term = $0.845(-1 + (a+b)P - abP^2)P = 0.845(-P + (a+b)P^2 - abP^3)$

The second term: $0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P = 0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$

Combining:
$$f(P) = 0.845(-P + (a+b)P^2 - abP^3) + 0.845P - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$$
$$= 0.845(a+b)P^2 - 0.845abP^3 - 0.845Pe^{-0.0969P}$$

So the GT has the form:
$$f(P) = \alpha P^2 + \beta P^3 + \gamma P e^{\delta P}$$

where $\alpha > 0$, $\beta < 0$, $\gamma < 0$, $\delta < 0$.

The **basis functions** present in GT are: $P^2$, $P^3$, and $Pe^{\delta P}$ (with $\delta < 0$).

Now let me check each candidate.
